```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- taichou: physical condition, state of health
- kibun: feeling, mood
- omou: to think, to consider
- omoide: memories, recollections
- omoi: thought, imagination

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- よくなった (yokunaru): to become better [Past tense]
- でも: even if (grammar pattern)
- おもいます (omou): to think [Polite/Formal form]
- わるくて (warui): bad [Te-form]
- たべられなかった (taberu): to eat [Potential / Passive, Negative, Past tense]

TONE HINT:
- genkyou: present condition

Input: sensei shonichi taichou yokunatta genki aru to でも omoimasu memai ga kibun warukute taberarenakatta
Output: /no_think
```

```
Output: I have chest pain.

Output: I have no allergies.
```

<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- genzai: the present, present time
- zensoku: asthma
- mansei: chronic illness
- haien: pneumonia
- genzai: original sin

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- なった (naru): to bear fruit [Past tense]
- こと: (you) should (grammar pattern)
- あります (aru): to be [Polite/Formal form]

TONE HINT:
- genjou: present condition

Input: genzai mata kako ni nikkan joutai ni natta こと arimasu ka zensoku mansei heisoku taishikan haien
Output: /no_think
```

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- mainichi: every day, daily
- shokku: shock emotional, shock physical
- gohan: cooked rice, meal
- gohan: lunch
- shokuji: meal, dinner

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- のんでます (nomu): to drink [Continuous (-te iru), Polite/Formal form]
- から: so / since (grammar pattern)
- いわれた (iu): to say [Passive, Want to do]
- ように: in order to / so that (grammar pattern)
- たべさせた (taberu): to eat [Causative, Want to do, Ki]
- でも: even if (grammar pattern)
- あまり: so / that (grammar pattern)
- たべられなくて (taberu): to eat [Potential / Passive, Negative, Te-form]
- なって (naru): to bear fruit [Te-form]
- だけ: as much as (grammar pattern)

TONE HINT:
- tabesugiru: to overeat

Input: hai asa no chouen shoku go mainichi nondemasu uchi gaikoukan から ketteiteki gohan wo iwaretayi ように tabesasetaki から でも saikin jibun あまり taberarenakute suguni yononaka ga ippai ni natte shimaimsu sukoshi taberu だけ de suguni
Output: /no_think
```

<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- sensei: teacher, instructor
- korera: cholera
- shukudai: homework, assignment
- kudasai: please give me, please do for me
- jugyouryou: tuition fee, course fee

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- わかった (wakaru): to understand [Past tense]
- いじょう: so long as (grammar pattern)
- わるkない (warui): bad [Negative]

TONE HINT:
- sukejuuru: schedule

Input: wakatta sensei korera いじょう warukunai kawaranai to iinokosu desu ga sugi no youyaku itsu desuka saisho chichi no hi de happyoukai aru no de
Output: /no_think
```
